  26. I have had this curling wand for 2 weeks now. I have a lot of experience with curling wands, so I thought I would weigh in, since most of the reviews on this product are from people who don't seem to have much knowledge about how to use them or what to expect.<br /><br />First off, this is a good quality curling wand. So far, I haven't noticed any \\"cheap\\" traits about it. It is not too expensive and is a great deal.<br /><br />Now a bit about wands in general for those who are new to them. Curling wands are not for inexperienced users! They are not \\"super easy\\" to use. That is why there are still curling irons with clamps still out there, for those who need the clamps. I have had 4 different brands/types of curling wands. All of mine came with gloves, which I never use because you need to be able to have a good hold on your hair to get the look you want. So if you learn how to hold and maneuver a curling wand, you do not need the glove.<br /><br />Second, these wands do give you a more natural and professional curl/wave, and can do so quickly, but it does take practice to achieve the goal. There are numerous types of curls, spirals and waves you can make with a wand and each one calls for a different technique.<br /><br />Third.....DO NOT get a curling wand that is multiple size barrel (like this one) IF you do not have experience with one. Start with a wand that is a one size barrel to learn and then gravitate to these. These multiple size barrels are great, they can change up the curls and waves nicely and make a more natural look, but because the barrel gets smaller on the way down, it does mean if you don't know how to use it, it can be frustrating and difficult to keep your hair even on it, without slipping....like I said practice makes perfect.<br /><br />Now for this particular wand, it is infused with real pearl...this is great, yes it makes the wand slippery! Now use logic and realize that the more slip and smoothness of the wand, the better for your hair.If you hair does not slip from a wand then you should be worried because that means your hair is sticking to the wand with the heat, by burning it.<br /><br />So if you buy this particular wand, understand that it is more slippery, I noticed that this wand does make my hair shine more and look more smooth and soft.<br /><br />I have extremely thick hair and a lot of it. My hair is naturally curly, but it is messy curly so I use wands to touch up my curls and make them nicer, similar to what Taylor Swift does. Now, even though my hair is natural curly, does not mean it is easy to curl with an iron. Since I have very long and thick hair, plus the large amount....it is very heavy and tends to weigh down, so curls tend to flatten easily. I have used this wand several times in the last two weeks....I did my hair early in the morning and went to an 8 hour shift of work. At the end of the day, my curls were still there and not frizzy.<br /><br />All in all, this wand is a great deal and perfect for someone looking for decent quality at a low price. Like I said, this particular style of wand needs some experience and/or practice.<br /><br />The bigger sized barrel of this wand is better for big loose spirals or beach waves hair styles. The smaller one would be better for tighter more Shirley Temple curls.<br /><br />If you are a beginner to curling wands, don't be discouraged, they are fantastic, but start with a one size barrel to learn.<br /><br />I will update my review in about 6-8 months to review the long term quality of this product. :)

I burned my fingers, and due to my lack of experience with curling irons I zinged my ears and neck a couple of times before calling it a day. I kept swapping between putting the glove on the left hand and the right and felt that that step was really cumbersome. The sort of problems I've never had to deal with before when using a flat iron. Needless to say I was a little disappointed after being psyched up to all the lovely reviews I'd read on this thing. I gave it another go this morning. The reviews stating that their hair held a curl even when sleeping on it were true. Normally, the morning after I flat-iron style my hair, it is all frizzy with squished curls. I woke to smooth curls just the way I left them when I went to bed. I went and got another glove, a roll of blue painter's tape and tried again. First off, if you are prone to burning yourself or have short hairs at the nape of your neck that you want to curl, lay a strip of tape across your bare skin at the nape of your neck. Take another short strip and fold it over the top of your ears, protecting the tip, sides and outward-facing aspect of your ear. Put on both gloves. Hold down the power button on your device to fire it up. Now you're ready to begin. Unlike the YouTube videos where gals were twirling long locks over the barrel, I have short hair so I sectioned, took a wide piece of hair and laid it over the barrel horizontally. With a gloved hand I smoothed it over the barrel as the other hand pulled the wand up. This helped me get a lot of volume at the roots, precisely what I bought this for. With two gloves, it is easy to alternate between hands to style. I felt less edgy and nervous that I'd burn myself. As clumsy and accident prone as I am, I did not burn myself once. And the nice thing is, if you apply the tape just right, you can reuse it again a few more times. The advantages over this curling wand over getting another CHI flat iron were that it was more affordable, damaged my hair less and had longer-lasting curls. The disadvantage was the burning part, but I figured a way around that. I picked up this larger barrel because I wanted to use it to volumize my hair, and it worked. Neat little styling tool! Very fast once you get the hang of it! I would have given a full 5 stars if it actually had two gloves instead of one.

If you want to go the extra mile, when the curl comes out, cup the curl in your hand for 5 sec. to really set it.

  350. I chose this curling iron after returning a highly rated clamp-style product from Hot Tools I had seen featured in women's magazines. For me, the clamp keep leaving indentations in my hair. I began researching for a wand (clamp-free) iron, and stumbled upon this Remington model that was highly rated by other Amazon reviewers. As suggested, I watched a few online tutorials to get the gist of wand curling techniques before my first use and I researched the temperature I should use. I concur with other reviewers that this is essential for new users to avoid frustration and unnecessary hair damage. I found that the default setting (356 degrees) for 10-12 sec was sufficient to set a typical curl from an approx. 1 inch wide lock of hair. As has been noted, it takes a few uses to get used to the grip of the wand: you really want to keep it nearly inverted. And I always use the heat-protection glove (included) to minimize singeing of my finger tip. For this reason, I would not recommend this product for all users (for example, tweens or adults with severe arthritis who might experience discomfort after repeatedly pinching a small lock of hair under tension). In the end, the wand delivered on its promise of loose, natural looking curls without the clamp marks. With the exception of my standard heat protectant (I use Tresemme or Bumble & Bumble), the curls held their shape for about 10 hours without any styling products. Not bad for 10-15 minutes of effort. By the end of the day, the curls were much looser, but still gave the hair some additional volume. My first attempt I did use the glove, and I'm glad because the wand is really awkward to use when you're not used to it, and I probably would have burned myself.<br /><br />I feel like the trick is to go behind your head with the wand on the opposite side from which you are curling. You have to wrap the hair TIGHTLY around the wand (with your gloved hand), with the wand facing down to get the best curl and hold it there for at least 5 seconds, if not more, depending on your hair. I started with a temp around 390, but had to go all the way up to 410 for my hair to hold the curl. I sprayed my whole head first with Aussie Sprunch spray, then brushed my hair. After curling one complete side I would again spray with hairspray and leave it. Once my whole head was done I resprayed my entire head, used my fingers to adjust the curls, then used a dry shampoo at the roots to give it more volume, and a shine spray. Sounds like a lot of effort, but the whole business took about 40 minutes, and I believe it will go faster once I start getting used to the process. I ended up with a nice head of loose curly waves with lots of volume, and those Kardashians girls had nothing on me.<br /><br />Bottom line, I would definitely purchase while keeping in mind that the first time may not be a success, so don't try it the morning before work. If the hair tends to slip off, use a hairspray first, then brush through your hair and it should help. This is good for those with long, or very thick hair that usually have difficulty getting curls, and the price is right.

  611. But if you've never used a curling WAND before (vs. a curling iron), you really need to go to youtube and find a video that works for you.<br /><br />There are a few tips that helped me a lot. My favorite ones came from monicasocal on Youtube; her video is named \\"Beachy curls/waves using Remington curling wand\\" if you want to google it.<br /><br />My hair is similar to hers, but not quite as long, and mine is maybe a bit thicker. The highlights: she suggested parting your hair into a low, middle and high level. She suggested STARTING the wand at your chin for your lower hair (bottom of your head, say, ear length); for the middle section, start curling at the top of your lip; and for the top, start curling at the bridge of your nose.<br /><br />I pretty much followed those directions, and yes, it turned out great. (monicasocal, thank you!)<br /><br />The thing about a curling wand you have to know is that you need the glove, and yes, you'll be holding the curl 20 or so seconds (varies with the heat you have the dial turned up to, and the texture of your hair.)<br /><br />Other youtube videos suggest shaking your hair; some suggest running your fingers through it to loosen the curls but not destroy the definition. Just remember to let the curls COOL before you touch them, or else you'll be coming the curl out.<br /><br />One last tip: when you look for a youtube video to show you how to do this and what your result might be, find a girl who has hair similar to yours. It makes the trial and error part a lot more trial and a lot less error!

With a not so great iron or no hairspray, my hair can easily fall from voluminous curls to completely flat. I'm sure this completely depends on the behavior of your hair as well as the tightness of the curls, so don't expect that to work for everyone!<br /><br />Tips:<br /><br />* PRACTICE with the heat off! You need some time to get the hang of it if you're new<br />* Section off your hair in 3-5 layers, dependent on how long/thick your hair is--not only does this help organize the style, it also helps build volume! I twist my hair and clip it on top of my head<br />* Work from back to front in each half section (left & right side) so your finished curls aren't blocking view of your uncurled hair<br />* Hairspraying after each half section works best for holding my hair<br />* Hair slips off? I hold the wand upside down (tapered end down) at a slight angle, more towards horizontal. I use the same hand for my entire head<br />* You can hold the (-) button until a lock icon shows up so it's ok to accidentally press buttons while you hold the wand<br /><br />For the reviewers who left a poor rating and complained that it burned your skin... did you expect a hot iron NOT to burn you if you touched it? Any working hot styling appliance will do the same to you. Come on, now!
